    function setAttributeOnload(object, attribute, val) {
      if(window.addEventListener) {
        window.addEventListener('load',
          function(){ object[attribute] = val; }, false);
      } else {
        window.attachEvent('onload', function(){ object[attribute] = val; });
      }
    }

             <div class="main section" id="main">
              <div class="widget Blog" id="Blog1">
               <div class="blog-posts hfeed">
                <!-- google_ad_section_start(name=default) -->
                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Monday, October 25, 2010
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <meta content="@activistpost" name="twitter:site"/>
                   <meta content="summary_large_image" name="twitter:card"/>
                   <meta content="http://www.activistpost.com/" name="twitter:domain"/>
                   <meta content="http://www.activistpost.com/2010/10/5-best-countries-to-escape-americas.html" name="twitter:url"/>
                   <meta content="5 Best Countries to Escape America's Decline" name="twitter:title"/>
                   <meta content="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTYsSoK-LI/AAAAAAAAEAw/iIW0iE4DhPA/s320/expats.jpg" name="twitter:image:src"/>
                   <meta content="http://www.activistpost.com/2010/10/5-best-countries-to-escape-americas.html" name="twitter:url"/>
                   <div class="post hentry">
                    <a name="8281453014990316499">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title">
                     <a href="http://www.activistpost.com/2010/10/5-best-countries-to-escape-americas.html">
                      5 Best Countries to Escape America's Decline
                     </a>
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content">
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTYsSoK-LI/AAAAAAAAEAw/iIW0iE4DhPA/s1600/expats.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;" target="_blank">
                       <img border="0" height="190" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTYsSoK-LI/AAAAAAAAEAw/iIW0iE4DhPA/s320/expats.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     <b>
                      <a href="http://www.activistpost.com/2010/10/5-best-countries-to-escape-americas.html">
                       Activist Post
                      </a>
                     </b>
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Okay, you're upset with the direction America is headed and you've been thinking of moving to another country. Perhaps you feel exhaustively cynical about the political, economic, or social situation in the U.S. and think it is beyond repair. You wouldn't be alone. Many
                     <a href="http://www.activistpost.com/2010/09/dramatically-poisonous-economy-heading.html">
                      top economists
                     </a>
                     and other trend forecasters are now openly predicting that a total economic, environmental, and social collapse may be imminent in America.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Americans, young professionals and baby boomers alike, are increasingly saying that their main desire for moving out of America is to seek "political asylum" of sorts. In the past, this political discontent was typically drawn along party lines -- under Bush's 8 years the exodus mainly consisted of bitter Democrats, while as recently as March Rush Limbaughdeclared, half-jokingly, that
                     <a href="http://www.examiner.com/political-buzz-in-national/video-rush-limbaugh-clarifies-pledge-to-move-to-costa-rica-if-health-care-bill-passes" target="_blank">
                      he'd move to Costa Rica
                     </a>
                     if "Obamacare" became law. However, these days, more Americans have grown cynical of the system itself and have given up on left-right politics.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Many believe that dropping out of the system as much as possible is the best form of protest. And now, because many people can telecommute through the Internet, it seems that living outside the U.S. is more do-able than ever. Furthermore, the lower cost of living in many other countries may actually increase the standard of living for some people.
                     <br/>
                     <a name="more">
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                      <script type="text/javascript">
                       &lt;!--
google_ad_client = "pub-1897954795849722";
/* 300x250, created 7/31/10 */
google_ad_slot = "8584321649";
google_ad_width = 300;
google_ad_height = 250;
//--&gt;
                      </script>
                      <br/>
                      <script src="http://pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/show_ads.js" type="text/javascript">
                      </script>
                     </div>
                     Surely, America will rebound from its eventual collapse, much like Russia and Argentina have, but it might make for uncomfortable sacrifices in America during the next decade. More Americans are looking to "ride out the storm" elsewhere, while others desire to become permanent nomads seeking foreign opportunity and adventure.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     It should be noted that no country is perfect and you'll face challenges no matter where you go. You'll find that modernization and rampant consumerism is expandinginto almost every corner of the world.  Some view this as a good thing, as more American comforts can be found, while others view it as a cultural blight to foreign lands. Your expectations must be kept realistic in that you may not find paradise, but your expat adventure may ultimately lead to a more peaceful lifestyle.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     The criteria for countries of safe haven include social stability, economic opportunity, freedom of self-expression, relative self-sufficiency, and an essential local community strength. These critical components are the foundation for living life with a greater sense of independence.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Here are our
                     <b>
                      5 best countries for Americans to escape the decline
                     </b>
                     :
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTZOdybnWI/AAAAAAAAEA0/c5NKzenVdKI/s1600/uruguay.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;" target="_blank">
                       <img border="0" height="239" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTZOdybnWI/AAAAAAAAEA0/c5NKzenVdKI/s320/uruguay.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     1.
                     <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uruguay" style="font-weight: bold;" target="_blank">
                      Uruguay
                     </a>
                     , whose official motto is "libertad o muerte (liberty or death)," is located in South America, southwest of Brazil and east of Argentina. Uruguay borders on the Atlantic Ocean and has developed infrastructure, a stable democracy, European flair, and rich culture that draws many expats to her borders.Uruguay is a constitutional democracy with one of the most developed economies in South America, possessing a high GDP per capita. Between the years 2007 and 2009, Uruguay was the only country in the Americas which didn't technically experience a recession, and now has the lowest Income Inequality and
                     <a href="http://investba.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/02/il2010.png" target="_blank">
                      highest Quality of Life in Latin America
                     </a>
                     , second only to Canada in all the Americas.Uruguay is rated as the least corrupt country in Latin America with its political and labour conditions being among the freest on the continent. In 2010, Uruguay became the first nation in Latin America to test hemp cultivation, while no drugs are illegal for personal consumption. Located entirely in the temperate zone, Uruguay provides an excellent climate for growing.
                     <br/>
                     <div style="margin: 0px;">
                      <br/>
                     </div>
                     Housing costs are much lower than the United States, as well as health care and food. Some consumer products such as cars and electronics can cost more, as well as Internet connection fees. Americans can buy real estate and own businesses, and they have an automatic 90-day visa to explore Uruguay. Americans only need to have a proof-of-income of
                     <a href="http://www.escapeartist.com/Special_Reports/Uruguay_Passport/Uruguay_Passport.pdf" target="_blank">
                      $500/mth to apply for residency
                     </a>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTaFFpYKqI/AAAAAAAAEA4/wFWbKFrWfAQ/s1600/costa-rica-sunset.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;" target="_blank">
                       <img border="0" height="240" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTaFFpYKqI/AAAAAAAAEA4/wFWbKFrWfAQ/s320/costa-rica-sunset.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     2.
                     <b>
                      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Costa_Rica" target="_blank">
                       Costa Rica
                      </a>
                     </b>
                     is a peaceful country in Central America, often referred to as the "Switzerland" of the Latin America due to its stable economy, political stability, and quality health care. Costa Rica, blessed with two beautiful coast lines (Pacific andCaribbean),is roughly the size of West Virginia and home to around 4 million people. The Central Valley's eternal springlike climate is said to be one of the best in the world allowing for a year-round growing season. Costa Rica is consistently voted one of the "
                     <a href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/environment/2009/jul/04/costa-rica-happy-planet-index" target="_blank">
                      Happiest and Greenest
                     </a>
                     " countries in the worldwith about 95% of its electric production coming from renewable sources. AARP and others have ranked itone of the
                     <a href="http://www.welovecostarica.com/public/AARP_Ranks_Atenas_Costa_Rica_One_of_The_Best_Places_to_Retire_Abroad.cfm">
                      best foreign retirement locations
                     </a>
                     ,as ithas all the same modern conveniences found in America and is only a 5-hour flight from New York.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Besides the price of real estate, which is comparable to the U.S., the cost of living is lower -- especially property taxes, health insurance, and fresh food. Americans have an automatic 90-day visa which can be renewed by leaving the country for 3 days before re-entering. Non-residents can own real estate and businesses, but are not allowed to work without a work visa. Residency requirements vary based on category. Current information is
                     <a href="http://arcr.net/residency/criteria.html" target="_blank">
                      available here
                     </a>
                     .
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTac-MrQEI/AAAAAAAAEA8/MbJfNgNVOSQ/s1600/new+zealand.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;" target="_blank">
                       <img border="0" height="241" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTac-MrQEI/AAAAAAAAEA8/MbJfNgNVOSQ/s320/new+zealand.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     3.
                     <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand" style="font-weight: bold;" target="_blank">
                      New Zealand
                     </a>
                     <b>
                     </b>
                     might be the most isolated fully developed nation in the world. It shares no borders, sits relatively distant from any other nation, has no real national enemies, has a safe democracy and a diverse landscape with many remote places to hide away within.Located in the South Pacific with beautiful beaches, sunshine, friendly people, and stunning vistas, it has two main islands and several smaller islands like Chatham Island and the Cook Islands. New Zealand ranks highly in international comparisons on many topics, including education, economic freedom, and lack of corruption. New Zealand now ranks among the
                     <a href="http://www.heritage.org/Index/Country/NewZealand" target="_blank">
                      freest economies in the world
                     </a>
                     with one of the least corrupt governments
                     <a href="http://www.visionofhumanity.org/wp-content/uploads/2010/06/2010-GPI-Results-and-Methodology-Report1.pdf" target="_blank">
                      ranked #1 on the Global Peace Index in 2010
                     </a>
                     -- second year in a row. Its cities also consistently rank among the
                     <a href="http://www.sbs.com.au/news/article/1025332/Aussie-cities-high-in-liveability-ranking" target="_blank">
                      world's most liveable
                     </a>
                     . The most commonly spoken language is English.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     The cost of living is somewhat comparable to the United States. Americans have an automatic 90-day visa to enter and explore the country. Non-residents can apply for a
                     <a href="http://www.immigration.govt.nz/" target="_blank">
                      2-year work visa
                     </a>
                     only in fields determined by immigration.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTbvY4cjNI/AAAAAAAAEBA/ylhNwaspu7g/s1600/iceland.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;" target="_blank">
                       <img border="0" height="236" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTbvY4cjNI/AAAAAAAAEBA/ylhNwaspu7g/s320/iceland.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     4.
                     <b>
                      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iceland" target="_blank">
                       Iceland
                      </a>
                     </b>
                     has a free market economy that has historically been one of the wealthiest and most developed nations in the world. In 2007, it was ranked as the most developed country in the world by the United Nations' Human Development Index, and the fourth most productive country per capitaeconomy. In 2008, Iceland's economy was devastated by the international bankers calling their foreign debt due. However, because of pride and solidarity among the people, strong social services, a nearly self-reliant energy sector, and amanageable population (320,000), it is poised to recover once the foreign debt issues are settled.Iceland has passed legislation to establish the country as a "
                     <a href="http://www.english.rfi.fr/europe/20100819-iceland-become-press-freedom-haven" target="_blank">
                      free speech haven
                     </a>
                     " to protect journalists and their sources. This law is a huge deal as most Western countries seem to be heading toward regulating the Internet, and it has the potential to jump-start the Icelandic economy in terms of offering censorship-free servers and other services to journalists and internet businesses. Iceland is also a peaceful country with no standing army.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     Iceland will be working it's way back from financial collapse, while the U.S. still appears headed for the cliff. Because of the shattered financial system, there are good opportunities to live on less income in Iceland now than during its peak, while all the signs seem poised for recovery. Residency hastraditionallybeen difficult to get in Iceland and is
                     <a href="http://www.iceland.is/people-and-society/People/ResidenceCitizenship/#Residence_Permits" target="_blank">
                      usually done through vital employment needs
                     </a>
                     , but the new push as a political safe-haven may open up the process a bit. Currently, American passports have an automatic 90-day visa to visit Iceland.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                      <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTc5BS6CSI/AAAAAAAAEBE/Fvj8m9a8YHc/s1600/Ushuaiacity.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;" target="_blank">
                       <img border="0" height="240" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_qLAIskTQXUc/TMTc5BS6CSI/AAAAAAAAEBE/Fvj8m9a8YHc/s320/Ushuaiacity.jpg" width="320"/>
                      </a>
                     </div>
                     5.
                     <b>
                      <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina" target="_blank">
                       Argentina
                      </a>
                     </b>
                     has bounced back from its financial collapse in 2002 when it defaulted on international debt causing massive inflation and high unemployment. The people said "Nunca Mas," the government has since paid off its debt to the IMF, and Argentina now has one of the
                     <a href="http://investba.com/wp-content/uploads/2010/02/il2010.png" target="_blank">
                      world's highest qualities of life
                     </a>
                     . Argentina is the second largest country in South America and the 8th largest in the world. It is a fully-developed country with strong agricultural production as the second-largest exporter of corn in the world -- not to mention good wines and beef too. The capital ofBuenos Aires is known as the Paris of Latin America because it feels like a European city with rich architecture and numerous sidewalk cafes. If the arts and ambiance with a low cost of living are your thing, then Argentina may be the best bang for your buck.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>
                     The cost of living is reportedly much lower than the United States for housing, food, travel, and health care. Americans have an automatic passport visa of 90 days to Argentina as well.
                     <a href="http://www.property-argentina.com.ar/visas_resident_permit_Argentina_real_estate/visas_resident_permit_Argentina_real_estate.html" target="_blank">
                      Pensioners
                     </a>
                     will need to prove a $700 per month income to qualify for residency, while others can apply if they prove a steady income of $900 per month.
                     <br/>
                     <br/>

                     </b>

                       <p>
                        Good article, followed by mindless, reactionary comments...
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I for one intend to stay in America and ride out the storm, but the best thing that can happen is that Americans start leaving America and warning other countries to fortify themselves against the same mistakes that America made. Change will not come from within America, anyone who thinks so is living a pipe dream, it does not matter who you elect.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        The reason America can export its destruction overseas is because the European and Asian nations are too fixated on their own racial and tribal feuds going back centuries if not millennia. America is a power simply because there is a power vacuum. If the nations of the world are too feeble to overcome their old prejudices and work together than perhaps a few American expats can snap them into line and make them realize what the stakes are.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I know a lot of people don't want to hear this, but when nations like France are thumbing their nose at us, even as they are reaping huge rewards from the corrupt economic order we defend, even as they are importing third world labor and repressing its natural traditions, even as they still can't get over their ancient hatreds of the Germans and the British, they look like a bunch of hypocritical parasites.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Wake up, this war had nothing to do with Bush and the Republicans! It was planned as early as 1998 by Clinton! It was fought to defend the very bedrock of our corrupt banking system! The Democrats allowed it to happen because they wanted to benefit from its spoils even as they used it as an election issue! Ditto for European leaders! If your nation has not overthrown its bankers and jailed them you are no better than America!

                       <p>
                        I cannot speak for Iceland, Uruguay, Costa Rica, or New Zealand. But Argentina is not exactly paradise.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Argentines are so distrustful of their economy that many use the USD for transactions. This has led to a spike in violent robberies often resulting in death in Buenos Aires. Thieves wait outside banks and have partners tell them via subtle signals who are the customers exiting banks with lots of cash on them.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Argentine politics are also notoriously corrupt, and many within the society openly deride President Cristina Kirchner and her husband as shamelessly corrupt.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Beef and wine are indeed of great quality - this cannot be disputed. But Americans will hardly come upon an enlightened, safe, or advanced society if they relocate to Argentina. Save for those very well off living in cloistered suburbs or small towns in the interior, Americans moving to Argentina will face typical 3rd world corruption, violence, and confusion/mess that can generally only be found in the most dangerous urban areas of the United States.

Uruguay is 3rd world country with first world prices. For some items, like major appliances or cars, prices are more than first world.
                       </p>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-5327826838287028293">
                       <p>
                        As for Argentina, I have made about 60 trips there over the years. First, let me say that Argentines may indeed own guns, but they must be registered, and are closely monitored by the government. Ammunition is scarce and very expensive. The purchase of ammunition is very closely regulated, in that one may purchase ammunition only for the calibers and/or gauges of guns he owns, and then only a very limited supply for each gun. Foreigners may easily import guns into the country, but the permit has a validity of only 90 days. And as for the much-rumored cheapness of Argentina, it's all a myth. Buenos Aires is just as expensive as New York or any other major world city. And inflation is running about 25--30% a year. A very pleasant place to visit for a few weeks, but to live there?
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-3745784707763313559">
                       <p>
                        The notion of global governance has taken an evolutionary path to the present day, with the principle global political and economic actors and institutions incrementally constructing the apparatus of a global government. In the modern world, global governance is an inter-lapping, intersecting, and intertwined web of international organizations, think tanks, multinational corporations, nations, NGOs, philanthropic foundations, military alliances, intelligence agencies, banks and interest groups. Globalization  a term which was popularized in the late 1980s to refer to the global spread of multinational corporations  has laid the principle ideological and institutional foundations for this process. Global social, economic and political integration do not occur at an equal pace; rather, economic integration and governance on a global level has and will continue to be ahead of the other sectors of human social interaction, in both the pace and degree of integration. In short, global economic governance will set the pace for social and political global governance to follow.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

More "vanilla|" or everyday corruption there is, the better it will be for survival purposes.

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-329835464588514414">
                       <p>
                        PART 2:
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        As to the 5 countries recommended to escape to, here is my take:
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        1. Uruguay is mostly farmland and flat.  The fact that is on the Atlantic Ocean and coastal, i.e., low elevation, is a negative if tsunami is a concern.  It is a third world nation with first world expenses as someone commented above.  Not recommended.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        2. Costa Rica.  Bi-coastal.  Too close to EEUU (the U.S. and the influence there of).  Countries like Chile, Columbia, and Peru have too much of American influence and presence in terms of military bases, military advisors, military troops, financial and economic "aid," etc.  If you are escaping from the "yankees," you might not want to relocate to these countries.  Not recommended.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        3. New Zealand.  See my comments above about English-speaking countries.  Not recommended.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        4. Iceland.  It is very remote and the population size is, what, 300,000?  Small population, but land mass and lots of geothermal energy sources (which could be good or bad).  The people there are stuck in some "Scandinavian" time-warp in terms of human relationships.  Read Michael Lewis' excellent article called "Wall Street on the Tundra" on Iceland at http://www.vanityfair.com/politics/features/2009/04/iceland200904.  Only recommended if you are of the Scandinavian stock.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        5. Argentina.  I have lived there for 2 years.  Argentina is a country of great contrast.  If you plan on moving there, you need to know where in Argentina you want to relocate to.  In Buenos Aires, there is too much people, crime, pollution, etc.  In the south, in the so-called "Lake District" is where you want to look.  Argentina is a country rich with natural resources (clean water, farmland, silver, agricultural products, etc.).  It takes a lot to fu*k up this beautiful country.  But remember the teaching on corruption above; it can work to your advantage if done properly.  Price inflation rate (food, fuel, salaries, things that normal people need to live and survive, etc.) in Argentina is between 25 to 30% per year.  That is one hell of an inflation rate!  However, if one knows how to grow clean, renewable energy (alcohol or ethanol) AND organic food in greenhouses in local communities, then inflation is not going to be a problem.  Recommended, but you need some expertise on people on the ground living and working in Argentina to help you.  Maybe I can help.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-4466761147577543054">
                       <p>
                        Try Malaysia.  I've lived in Penang for 2.5 years on a tourist visa.  The crime is almost non-existent, food is cheap, rentals cheap, accommodating police to foreigners (Westerners only), village living or city.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        The weather is warm, but not too hot.  The people are as friendly as they come.  The Muslim religion practiced by the Malays is rather liberal, too.  Electricity and water costs are a joke!  Good Internet connection and stable power that you'd find in the West.  Healthcare is top notch and cheap!
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        From here, all of Asia is a quick jaunt, too.  Ninety-day visa can be renewed over and over by skipping into Thailand and back within six hours by bus.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Penang has cheap places (but not seedy) to live and luxurious places to live, cheap restaurants and expensive ones--though the expensive ones are cheap by Western fare.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-6419104833111969474">
                       <p>
                        As a hint to readers, first look for what is referred to as Purchasing Power Parity (PPP) of a country to assess affordability.  High PPP countries will resemble the US in many ways.  Low PPP countries are third-world, carrying with it inconveniences and most likely a higher threat of crime.  Look for PPP countries somewhere between $15,000 per capita to $25,000 per capita, then go from there.  Consider many Muslim countries, as the propaganda from the West about Muslims is truly off the wall.  I know; I've lived among Malays, and I'll tell you, they are fine people with excellent moral values and sense of community.  and the best part is that they're not interested in talking about their faith unless you ask.  I highly recommend Malaysia (not KL or other big cities) as a first stop to acclimate to Asia.  It's a good place, especially Penang, to call home while exploring the rest of Asia.
                       </p>

                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Whoah whoah whoah, watch your generalities there, buddy. Some of us have fought the ridiculous policies of our government from the start. Some of us are non-partisan and try our best to live not as good Americans, but good human beings. I, for instance, am very much an isolationist except when it comes to international aid and disaster relief. If I've spent 10 or 15 years of my life trying to fight against the tide of my own peers and their ridiculous desire to legislate stupid stuff like sexuality, why shouldn't I have the right to try and make a difference somewhere else? Smart Americans don't export their entire country when they move, which seems to be the sentiment I'm seeing from a lot of other posters - they don't want American citizens bringing their economic habits and other bad juju with them to a new home. I'd never do that. Some of us don't want to live like the rest of our countrymen do.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        So what's wrong with a citizen of the world trying to build a life and make a difference somewhere else? A lot of people here are too young to have voted the past few administrations into power, and so their stake in the entire mess is very delicate. How do they finish "their" mistakes if they didn't set them into motion?
                       </p>

                        It is the government, racism, religion [which, yes, I know is everywhere] that is screwing up America. Mainly the government and the politics but it is the people that is voting the politics in; therefore the people are partially to blame too, please stop trying to put the blame elsewhere when all of us are to blame here. Nobody is innocent in this, I know nobody wants to be at fault and maybe nobody is purposely but everyone has a little fault here, including myself, as I am American too. Those in government were average ordinary people at one time but they got corrupted when they got money and power. I have tried to stay optimistic about the outcome but this country is doomed and if it does get back on track, it will be at least a few generations down the road. I would guess at least a few generations down the road and maybe I am being cynical, I will admit, but who can blame me?
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Even if I am, it will definitely be no time in our lifetime and probably no time in our children's lifetimes either. Maybe in our grandchildren's lifetimes but that's just being generous and that is a big 'IF'.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        This is precisely why I am considering moving out of the country myself. Why stay in a country that my politicians refuse to listen to me in? A country that my children can't be proud of?
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Advice for those trying to move:
                        <br/>
                        I would have to check my funds of course and word of advice to anyone considering it, save up the proper funds before you move. Also realize no country is perfect, you're never going to find a country without faults, every country will have its problems. You just have to figure out which ones you're willing to compromise with. Do your research on your preferred country first too, don't just move because it's 'pretty' or it 'seems' nice. You may be surprised when you get there if you know nothing about the country. If it's a country that has a different culture and language than your own, obviously learn about the culture and language before you make the move. Visiting first is ideal but if you cannot do that, look at places online, look at jobs online, have a nice sized fund setup [doesn't have to be the size of a rich person but it does have to be a good sized one because you may not find a job right away and you will have to work]. Plan ahead of time, don't do everything last minute and follow the necessary procedures it may take to move to whichever country it is you're attempting to move to.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        -
                        <br/>
                        I'm not saying America is the worst place in the world, oh no, there's much worse. I'm just saying I am losing hope in it and I am considering leaving it, and I do not want my children growing only to be disappointed just as most are. I am not encouraging anyone else to, nor am I saying you shouldn't, but merely giving advice for those who decide they might want to.
                       </p>

Does the PRIDE of the 'haves' flaunting their material wealth and lavish lifestyles cause others ENVY, or is the ENVY first that causes one to LUST after something, acquire it and then feel the PRIDE of that?  I actually sit atop the science/religion fence but America seems bent on convincing the rest of the planet that we are primarily a CHRISTIAN based nation, yet seem to revel in committing the most foul sins ever written about!  Wow, I just don't understand why more of the 99% can't see this blatant sanctimonious hypocrisy and just decide once and for all to stop living this way and STOP FUNDING THE ULTRA-RICH LIFESTYLE FOR OTHERS!
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-8805907032809914681">
                       <p>
                        I have spent 14 years in the US and only got green card this year (yeah, this is how long it may take the "legal" way). I went to two graduate schools and earned two advanced degrees from US colleges, yet I have never made more than 19K a year - and that was my graduate stipend. Never been arrested, dammit! :) Apparently this is how much it's all valued here!  I was once a young, impressionable kid, but over the years of neglect and abuse became as cynical as Emperor Palpatine. Remember, there's no health care here - I can't call health market health care. This realization (and the fact that I am now approaching 40) makes me think it's time for another quantum leap - to get out of here and find a better place.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I have no intent to share the UGLIEST collective karma the US system has earned - I do not owe them anything. I am not a pussy, Mr. Icelander. I simply wasn't born here, so I lack that irrationally emotional part called patriotism.
                       </p>

                  function recentpostslist(json) {
 document.write('&lt;ul&gt;');
 for (var i = 0; i &lt; json.feed.entry.length; i++)
 {
    for (var j = 0; j &lt; json.feed.entry[i].link.length; j++) {
      if (json.feed.entry[i].link[j].rel == 'alternate') {
        break;
      }
    }
var entryUrl = "'" + json.feed.entry[i].link[j].href + "'";//bs
var entryTitle = json.feed.entry[i].title.$t;
var item = "&lt;li&gt;" + "&lt;a href="+ entryUrl + '" target="_blank"&gt;' + entryTitle + "&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/li&gt;";
 document.write(item);
 }
 document.write('&lt;/ul&gt;');
 }
